The Third Proof: Success from Weakness as Divine Confirmation
Imam al-Nasafi enumerates the third proof of prophethood: the Prophet's rise in weakness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's rise from poverty and weakness, without any human support, to overcome all opposition is a compelling proof of prophethood, demonstrating divine assistance.

Core Idea
The Prophet's victory in weakness proves his mission was divinely supported.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the third proof of prophethood: the Prophet Muhammad's seemingly impossible rise against the entire world while he was poor, weak, and had few supporters. His success despite all odds, and the failure of his powerful enemies to stop him, points to a source beyond human capability. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Set the scene: the Prophet's initial weakness
Notice the description: he was in a state of weakness, poverty, need, and had very few supporters. He rose as a war against all people.
This contrast is essential—he had no worldly power.
2
Examine the opposition
His enemies were kings, tyrants, and his own relatives. They demanded compromise but he refused. They used all their strength to stop him.
The enmity was religious, the severest kind.
3
Observe the outcome despite their efforts
Despite their best efforts, his followers only increased, his call spread, and his power consolidated. This was not due to human aid.
He was an orphan with no wealth or army.
4
Draw the conclusion: divine assistance
The author argues that such success from such weakness is proof of divine support and heavenly aid, and that he was aided by being feared.
This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث : أنه انتصب في حال ضعفه وفقره وفاقته وقلة أعوانه حربًا لجميع أهل الأرض ومتعرضا للملوك والجبارين وذوي القدرة والبسطة، وعاداهم معاداة الدين، وهي أشد أنواع العداوة، وسفه أحلامهم وأحلام آبائهم الذين كانوا يعتادون التفاخر بمآثرهم ومناقبهم ، وكان أشد الناس عليه عشيرته الأقربون ورهطه الأدنون، ولم يأخذه في الله لومة لائم، وطلبوا منه أدنى مداهنة ليتابعوه وأيسر مسايلة لينقادوا له، فلم يعطهم ذلك ولم يساعدهم عليه، ثم إنهم مع قوة أبدانهم وكثرة عددهم ووفور عددهم أتوا بأقصى ما في وسعهم من الجد والاجتهاد واستعمال العدة والعتاد لإطفاء نوره وطمس آثاره فلم يزدد ذلك إلا كثرة الأتباع وقوة الأشياع وانتشار الدعوة وشد الشوكة من غير أن كان ذلك راجعا إلى معونة بشرية على ما عليه أمر طلاب دول الدنيا المعتمدين في ذلك على كثرة الأموال وقوة الأنصار والأعوان، بل كان نشأ يتيمًا لا تبع له وعائلاً لا مال له، وهذا من أول الدلائل على أن أمره كان مبنيًا على المعونة الإلهية والتأييد السماوي، ولهذا بالرعب وكان يُخاف منه مسيرة شهر.
The third: that he rose in a state of his weakness, poverty, need, and scarcity of supporters as a war against all the people of the earth, exposing himself to kings, tyrants, and those possessing power and authority, and he opposed them with the enmity of religion, which is the severest kind of enmity, and he regarded as foolish their minds and the minds of their fathers who used to boast of their exploits and virtues. And the severest people against him were his closest relatives and his nearest kin, and no blame of a blamer affected him in [the cause of] God. And they asked from him the slightest compromise so that they might follow him, and the easiest concession so that they might submit to him, but he did not give them that and did not assist them in it. Then, despite the strength of their bodies, the multitude of their numbers, and the abundance of their number, they came with the utmost of their effort and striving and use of equipment and weapons to extinguish his light and efface his traces, but that only increased the multitude of followers, the strength of partisans, the spread of the call, and the consolidation of power, without that being due to human assistance as is the case of seekers of worldly kingdoms who rely in that on abundance of wealth and strength of supporters and helpers. Rather, he grew up as an orphan with no followers and a poor man with no wealth. And this is among the first proofs that his affair was based on divine assistance and heavenly support, and because of this [he was aided] by terror and he was feared from a month's journey.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof of prophethood. The author describes how the Prophet Muhammad, despite being weak, poor, in need, and with few supporters, rose as a war against all the people of the earth, challenging kings and tyrants. He did so with religious enmity, which is the most severe, and he regarded their ancestral boasts as foolish. His closest relatives were his fiercest opponents, yet he did not fear blame. They asked for the slightest compromise but he refused. Despite their strength and numbers, they tried to extinguish his light but only increased his followers and the spread of his call, without any human support. He was an orphan and poor. This demonstrates that his mission was based on divine assistance and heavenly support, and he was aided by terror (being feared from a month's distance). The author argues that such success from such weakness is a clear proof of prophethood.

Key Terms
انتصب
معونة إلهية
تأييد سماوي
رعب
دعوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's success was due to his own strategy, wealth, or human resources.
Correction: The passage explicitly states he was an orphan with no followers and no wealth, and his success came without human assistance, indicating divine support.

Checkpoint
What does the author cite as evidence that the Prophet's rise was based on divine assistance?
A) His wealth and supporters
B) His miraculous eloquence
C) His success despite being a weak orphan with no human aid
D) His lineage

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's rise from weakness to triumph, unaided by human means, is a clear sign that his mission was divinely supported.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face opposition or feel powerless in your faith, do you truly believe that divine support can bring about success without any worldly resources? How does the Prophet's example challenge your tendency to rely on your own strength?
?
The Prophet refused to compromise even under pressure from his own family. Are there areas in your life where you compromise your faith for the sake of peace or approval? What would it take for you to adopt the same unwavering stance?
?
The Prophet's success came from weakness, not from accumulation of wealth or numbers. What does this tell you about how Allah measures success? In your own life, what are you building your confidence upon—worldly means or divine support?

The Prophet's Steadfastness: Proof of Prophethood
Author presents the fourth proof: the Prophet's endurance of hardships and rejection of worldly temptations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unwavering constancy in both hardship and prosperity serves as a rational proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Consistency in asceticism through poverty and power proves the Prophet's truthfulness.

This passage presents the fourth of several proofs that the Prophet Muhammad is truly a messenger of God. The author argues that no impostor or person seeking personal gain could maintain such perfect consistency in asceticism and patience through both extreme hardship and later worldly success. This remarkable constancy points to a higher source of motivation: sincere insight and complete trust in Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation. Let the narrative of the Prophet's two phases (hardship and prosperity) sink in before you interpret.
Notice the shift in conditions but the unchanged behavior.
2
Identify the two phases of the Prophet's life
The passage describes two distinct periods: the early Meccan period of suffering and rejection, and the later Madinan period of political power and wealth. Find where this shift occurs in the text.
The key transition is marked by 'ثم لما استقامت له الأمور' (Then when affairs became steady for him).
3
Observe the Prophet's consistency across both phases
Note that the author emphasizes the Prophet's constancy (وتيرة واحدة) in both periods. He did not change his ascetic lifestyle or seek worldly pleasures even when they were within his reach.
The Prophet continued in humility and patience even after gaining power.
4
Understand the implication
The author argues that such consistency cannot be explained by ordinary motives like personal ambition or love of comfort. It proves the Prophet's truthfulness and his sincere insight and trust in Allah.
The final sentence ties the Prophet's behavior to his creation for the eternal abode.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرابع أنه عليه السلام تحمل في إظهار دعوته المشاق التي لا خفاء بمكانها، والمتاعب التي ليست في الجملة البشرية احتمالها فدام في ذلك كله على وتيرة واحدة لا يسأم عن شأنه ولا يمل عن دعوته، وعرضت عليه المطامع من الثروة والرياسة ليترك دعوته فلم يجبهم إلى ذلك بل قال : وَمَا أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ وصبر على تلك المشاقات مترددًا في البؤس والفاقة منصرفًا في الضراء واللأواء صابرًا على شظف العيش ، ثم لما استقامت له الأمور وخضعت لدعوته الجمهور وضربت وفود العرب من السهل والجبل إلى بابه أكباد الأبل، وحملت إليه الأموال الجمة والعقد النفيسة، وصفت له جزيرة العرب بأسرها وخلصت عمن يعاديه وخلت عمن ينازعه ويناوئه فيها ، استمر على وتيرته، وداوم على التمسك بطريقته من ترك الاستمتاع بصنوف الملاذ الشهوية والإعراض عما هو دأب طلاب الملك من إحراز النعم الدنيوية، بل صبر على ما كان عليه من التباؤس والاستكانة والتجرع لمضض الفقر والفاقة، ولا يتوهم ذلك بلا بصيرة صادقة وثقة بربه تامة بل كل ذلك لما أكرمه الله تعالى وخلقه لدار كرامته التي أعدت للنعم التي لا يكدرها خوف الزوال ولا ينغصها شوب المطال، والله ذو المن والإفضال.
And the fourth: that he, peace be upon him, endured in making his call known the hardships whose place is not hidden, and the difficulties that are not in human capacity to bear, and he remained throughout all of that on one constant course, not tiring of his affair nor wearying of his call. And worldly temptations of wealth and leadership were presented to him to abandon his call, but he did not respond to them; rather he said: 'And I do not ask you for any reward for it.' And he endured those hardships, fluctuating in misery and poverty, turning in adversity and distress, patient in harsh living. Then when affairs became steady for him, the masses submitted to his call, the delegations of Arabs from plain and mountain struck the humps of camels to his door, abundant wealth and precious necklaces were brought to him, the whole Arabian Peninsula became pure for him, cleared of those who opposed him and empty of those who disputed and contended with him in it, he continued on his course, and persisted in adhering to his way of abandoning enjoyment of various sensual delights and turning away from what is the habit of seekers of kingship of acquiring worldly blessings. Rather, he remained patient on what he was of humility, lowliness, and swallowing the pain of poverty and need. And one should not imagine that without sincere insight and complete trust in his Lord; rather all of that was because God honored him and created him for the abode of His generosity which is prepared for blessings that fear of cessation does not disturb nor the admixture of taint spoil. And God is the possessor of favor and bounty.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof of prophethood. The author describes the Prophet's endurance of immense hardships in proclaiming his call, hardships beyond normal human capacity. He remained constant, not wearying. When offered wealth and leadership to abandon his call, he refused, quoting the Quran. He continued in poverty and distress. Then when he succeeded and gained power and wealth, he did not change his ascetic way but persisted in humility and patience. This consistency in both adversity and prosperity shows his truthfulness and complete trust in God, proving his prophethood. The author warns against attributing this to anything other than sincere insight and divine honor.

Key Terms

وتيرة واحدة
زهد
بصيرة صادقة
ثقة بالله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet changed his lifestyle after gaining political power, indulging in worldly pleasures like other rulers.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the Prophet continued on the same ascetic path after gaining wealth and power, avoiding sensual delights and remaining humble.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the Prophet do when offered wealth and leadership to abandon his call?
A) He accepted but only after negotiations
B) He refused and quoted the Quran
C) He considered but then declined
D) He ignored the offers

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unwavering asceticism and patience in both extreme poverty and worldly success prove his prophethood and sincere trust in Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve success, do you become attached to the comforts and status it brings? How does the Prophet's example—continuing in asceticism even after gaining power—expose the areas where you seek security in this world rather than in Allah? What would it cost you to live with that same detachment?
?
Consider a time when you faced hardship and were tempted to compromise your principles for an easier path. Did you hold firm? The Prophet refused offers of wealth and leadership to abandon his message. In your daily struggles, what small compromises do you make that, if unchecked, reveal a lack of sincere insight?
?
The Prophet's consistency was rooted in his complete trust in Allah's promise of an eternal reward that 'fear of cessation does not disturb.' If you truly believed that Allah has prepared for you something that never fades, how would your anxiety about money, reputation, or control change? What step can you take today to act on that belief?

The Proof from the Prophet's Noble Lineage
Author argues that the Prophet's lineage fulfills Abraham's prayer and is the purest of the Arabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet Muhammad's lineage serves as a proof of his prophethood, specifically as the fulfillment of Abraham's prayer and as the purest Arab lineage.

Core Idea
Muhammad's lineage fulfills Abraham's prayer and is the purest of the Arabs.

This passage presents a key proof of prophethood: the Prophet's noble lineage. The author argues that Muhammad (peace be upon him) was the direct answer to Abraham's prayer for a messenger from his descendants. Furthermore, his genealogy is traced through the most honorable ancestors, establishing his pure Arab lineage. This serves as a supporting evidence for his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation, noting the two main parts: the argument from Abraham's prayer and the genealogy list.
The passage begins with the prayer reference and ends with the list of ancestors.
2
Understand the argument from prayer
Identify how the author uses Abraham's Quranic prayer to claim that Muhammad is the only prophet from Ishmael's descendants, thus fulfilling that prayer.
The author quotes the verse and asserts no other prophet came from Ishmael's line.
3
Trace the lineage
Follow the list of ancestors from Ishmael down to 'Abd al-Muttalib. Note the descriptive words like 'grandchild', 'noble', 'pure', etc.
Each ancestor is given a specific honorific.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why lineage is used as a proof. It supports the credibility of the Prophet by connecting him to noble ancestry and to Abraham's prayer.
This is a supporting proof, not the primary basis for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما هو راجع إلى نسبه الشريف] وأما ما هم راجع إلى نسبه عليه السلام فإنه كان دعوة إبراهيم عليه السلام على ما أخبر الله خبرًا عن إبراهيم أنه قال: رَبَّنَا وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُمْ ) والهاء عائدة إلى ذريته وذرية إسماعيل عليه السلام فإن في صدر الآية: ﴿وَإِذْ يَرْفَعُ إِبْرَاهِمُ الْقَوَاعِدَ مِنَ الْبَيْتِ﴾ إلى أن قال : ﴿وَاجْعَلْنَا مُسْلِمَيْنِ لَكَ وَمِن ذُرِّيَّتِنَا أُمَّةً مُّسْلِمَةٌ لَكَ﴾ ثم قال ﴿وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُمْ﴾ ولا نبي من ولد إسماعيل عليه السلام إلا نبينا محمد سيد البشر ، ثم إنه عليه السلام كان حفدة إسماعيل، ونجل معد بن عدنان ونجيب مدر بن نذار، وسليل النضر بن كنانة، وأورع بني لؤي بن غالب، ولباب قصي بن كلاب، وصريح عبد مناف، وصفوة عمرو العلي وهو هاشم، وخلاصة عبد المطلب
What pertains to his noble lineage: And as for what pertains to his lineage, peace be upon him, it was the prayer of Abraham, peace be upon him, as God informed about Abraham that he said: 'Our Lord, and send among them a messenger from themselves.' And the pronoun refers to his descendants and the descendants of Ishmael, peace be upon him, for at the beginning of the verse: 'And when Abraham was raising the foundations of the House' until he said: 'And make us both Muslims to You and from our descendants a Muslim nation to You.' Then he said: 'And send among them a messenger from themselves.' And there is no prophet from the children of Ishmael, peace be upon him, except our Prophet Muhammad, the master of mankind. Then he, peace be upon him, was the grandchild of Ishmael, the son of Ma'add bin 'Adnan, the noble of Mudar bin Nizar, the descendant of al-Nadr bin Kinana, the most pious of Banu Lu'ayy bin Ghalib, the core of Qusayy bin Kilab, the pure of 'Abd Manaf, the elite of 'Amr al-'Ali who is Hashim, and the quintessence of 'Abd al-Muttalib.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents a proof of prophethood from lineage. The author argues that the Prophet Muhammad was the answer to Abraham's prayer for a messenger from among his descendants. Since the Prophet came from the lineage of Ishmael, and no other prophet came from Ishmael's children, this identifies him as that promised messenger. Then the author lists the Prophet's pure and noble ancestry, emphasizing that he is from the most honorable lineage of the Arabs, each ancestor being a notable figure. This purity of lineage adds to the proof of his prophethood.

Correction: Here lineage is a supporting proof, not the primary basis. Prophethood is granted by Allah's choice.

The Prophet's Steadfast Patience Despite Victory and Wealth
Nasafi describes the Prophet's steadfast patience despite poverty even after his mission succeeded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet Muhammad's patience remained constant even after his mission succeeded, and how his austerity was a sign of sincere trust in Allah.

Core Idea
The Prophet's poverty was chosen, not imposed; his patience proved his sincerity.

Nasafi presents a striking portrait of the Prophet's character. After his mission triumphed and he gained power and wealth, he did not change his simple way of life. This passage explains why: his patience was not weakness but profound trust in Allah's eternal reward.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the contrast between the two phases of the Prophet's life.
2
Identify the two phases
The passage describes the Prophet's life before and after his mission's success. Find the descriptions of hardship and then of victory.
The shift occurs after 'then when matters became stable for him'.
3
Notice what did not change
Despite acquiring wealth and authority, the Prophet continued his austere lifestyle. Identify the phrases that describe his continued patience and simplicity.
Keywords: 'continued on his pace', 'persisted in adhering to his way'.
4
Understand the reason given
Nasafi explains that the Prophet's behavior was due to sincere insight and complete trust in Allah, and because he sought the eternal blessings of the Hereafter.
This refutes any misunderstanding that he was forced or without reason.
5
Reflect on the lesson for prophethood
Consider how this shows the Prophet's character as a model of sincerity and trust in Allah, and why this is important in Islamic theology.
This connects to the broader purpose of prophethood: to guide by example.

صابرًا على شظف العيش، ثم لما استقامت له الأمور وخضعت لدعوته الجمهور وضربت وفود العرب من السهل والجبل إلى بابه أكباد الأبل، وحملت إليه الأموال الجمة والعقد النفيسة، وصفت له جزيرة العرب بأسرها وخلصت عمن يعاديه وخلت عمن ينازعه ويناوئه فيها، استمر على وتيرته، وداوم على التمسك بطريقته من ترك الاستمتاع بصنوف الملاذ الشهوية والإعراض عما هو دأب طلاب الملك من إحراز النعم الدنيوية، بل صبر على ما كان عليه من التباؤس والاستكانة والتجرع لمضض الفقر والفاقة، ولا يتوهم ذلك بلا بصيرة صادقة وثقة بربه تامة بل كل ذلك لما أكرمه الله تعالى وخلقه لدار كرامته التي أعدت للنعم التي لا يكدرها خوف الزوال ولا ينغصها شوب المطال، والله ذو المن والإفضال.
Patient in hardship of living, then when matters became stable for him and the masses submitted to his call and the delegations of Arabs from the easy and the difficult came to his door on the humps of camels, and abundant wealth and precious necklaces were brought to him, and the entire Arabian peninsula became pure for him and cleared of those who opposed him and emptied of those who contended with him therein, he continued on his pace and persisted in adhering to his way of abandoning enjoyment of varieties of sensual pleasures and turning away from what is the habit of seekers of kingship of acquiring worldly blessings; rather, he endured what he had been upon of destitution and humility and swallowing the bitterness of poverty and need. And let no one imagine that without sincere insight and complete trust in his Lord; rather, all that was because Allah Almighty honored him and created him for the abode of His generosity which is prepared for blessings that the fear of passing does not trouble nor the admixture of resentment spoil. And Allah is the possessor of bounty and grace.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage describes the Prophet's remarkable patience and consistency. It begins by acknowledging that before his mission, the Prophet endured hardship. Then, after his mission succeeded and he gained wealth, power, and authority over all of Arabia, he did not change his lifestyle. He continued to avoid worldly pleasures and remained in a state of humility and poverty. This proves his sincerity and complete trust in Allah, as he only sought the eternal blessings of the Hereafter. The passage emphasizes that his behavior was not a lack of insight but rather a sign of true faith.

Key Terms

شظف العيش
بصيرة صادقة
ثقة بربه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's later comfort and wealth meant that his early patience was no longer needed or that he became less patient.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the Prophet remained constant in austerity even after victory, proving that his patience was a continuous virtue rooted in trust in Allah, not a temporary response to difficulty.

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet continue to live in austerity even after gaining wealth and power?
A) He was forced to do so by his companions.
B) He lacked ability to enjoy worldly blessings.
C) He was motivated by sincere insight and trust in Allah's eternal reward.
D) He was merely imitating previous prophets without reason.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's consistent austerity after victory demonstrates that his patience was a profound act of faith, not a circumstantial response.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience comfort, success, or even abundance, do your priorities shift toward worldly pleasures and status, or do you remain anchored in patience and trust in Allah as the Prophet did? What specific habits or practices could you adopt to mirror his consistency?
?
The Prophet's poverty was a deliberate choice based on 'sincere insight' and 'complete trust'—not a sign of weakness. Where in your own life are you relying on material security or social approval instead of placing your full trust in Allah? What is one step you can take today to transfer that trust from the created to the Creator?
?
If you truly believed that your honor and eternal blessings lie in the Hereafter, would you still chase after fleeting satisfactions and resent your present hardships? How can you begin to view your current struggles as opportunities to cultivate that same sincere insight and trust?

The Prophet's Noble Lineage from Ibrahim's Prayer
Nasafi proves the Prophet's noble lineage from Ibrahim's prayer and his ancestors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's noble lineage, traced back to Ibrahim's supplication, serves as a proof of his prophethood and truthfulness.

Core Idea
The Prophet's lineage is not just noble; it is the direct answer to Ibrahim's prayer.

Nasafi begins by grounding the Prophet's ancestry in the supplication of Ibrahim (Quran 2:129). He then traces the noble lineage through specific ancestors, emphasizing their virtues. Finally, he argues that such a lineage—filled with leaders and men of honor—makes it impossible that the Prophet would fabricate his message. This lesson examines that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally before you interpret.
Notice the Quranic quotation and the long list of names.
2
Identify the supplication link
Find how Nasafi connects the Prophet to Ibrahim's prayer. He quotes Quran 2:129 and explains that the pronoun refers to Ishmael's descendants.
This is the first proof: the Prophet was prayed for by Ibrahim.
3
Reflect on the argument from nobility
After the genealogy, Nasafi argues that a person of such noble lineage could not possibly fabricate a message, as that trait belongs to base lineages.
This is a rational proof for his truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هم راجع إلى نسبه الشريف فإنه كان دعوة إبراهيم عليه السلام على ما أخبر الله خبرًا عن إبراهيم أنه قال: رَبَّنَا وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُمْ والهاء عائدة إلى ذريته وذرية إسماعيل عليه السلام فإن في صدر الآية: ﴿وَإِذْ يَرْفَعُ إِبْرَاهِمُ الْقَوَاعِدَ مِنَ الْبَيْتِ إلى أن قال : وَاجْعَلْنَا مُسْلِمَيْنِ لَكَ وَمِن ذُرِّيَّتِنَا أُمَّةً مُّسْلِمَةٌ لَكَ ثم قال وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُم ولا نبي من ولد إسماعيل عليه السلام إلا نبينا محمد سيد البشر، ثم إنه عليه السلام كان حفدة إسماعيل، ونجل معد بن عدنان ونجيب مدر بن نذار، وسليل النضر بن كتانة، وأورع بني لؤي بن غالب، ولباب قصي بن كلاب، وصريح عبد مناف، وصفوة عمرو العلي وهو هاشم، وخلاصة عبد المطلب وهو شبيه الحمد، ومن قبل أمهات آبائه متصلاً بمضاض بن عمرو الجرهمي جد ذكورة ولد إسماعيل وبأخواله من الخزرج بسلمى والدة عبد المطلب وبني زهرة بأمه آمنة، وله عليه السلام أنساب شريفة من قبل أمهات آبائه كالعواتك والفواطم وغيرهن، ثم لا يخفى على العلماء بالتواريخ والحفاظ لأنساب العرب وأيامها العارفين بأشرافهم وأجوادهم وشجعانهم أن كل واحد ممن يتصل نسبه به، كان عمادًا لأسرته ورئيسًا لقبيلته وزمرته وسيدًا لعشيرته مخصوصا بجميع الفضائل موصوفًا بالمحامد والمناقب، وكانوا أرباب الحكم والرفادة، وأصحاب السقاية والسدانة، وسادة دار الندوة، والوافدين عند الملوك والأجلة المعظمين في أعينهم المتبجلين عندهم المسمين عند جميع قبائل العرب - قحطانها وعدنانها مضرها وربيعها قيسها وخندقها آل الله وجيرانه وسكان حرمه ومن كان حال نسبه هذه الحالة، وعرقه في الشرف هذا العرق كان الاشتغال منه بالرزق والافتعال من الممتنع الذي لا تصور له والمحال الذي لا مجال له في العقول لثبوته إذ ذلك فعل من يرجع إلى خساسة في الأصل وضعة في النسب ولؤم في الأعراق ودناءه في الأخلاق، وبالله التوفيق.
As for what relates to his noble lineage, it was the supplication of Abraham, peace be upon him, as Allah informed us of Abraham that he said: 'Our Lord, and send among them a messenger from themselves' and the pronoun refers to his offspring and the offspring of Ishmael, peace be upon him, for in the beginning of the verse: 'And when Abraham was raising the foundations of the House... until he said: 'And make us both Muslims to You and from our descendants a Muslim nation to You.' Then he said: 'And send among them a messenger from themselves.' And there is no prophet from the children of Ishmael except our Prophet Muhammad, the master of mankind. Then he, peace be upon him, was the grandson of Ishmael, the son of Ma'add ibn 'Adnan, the noble son of Mudar ibn Nizar, the descendant of al-Nadr ibn Kinana, the most pious of the sons of Lu'ayy ibn Ghalib, the core of Qusayy ibn Kilab, the pure of 'Abd Manaf, the elite of 'Amr al-'Ali who is Hashim, and the essence of 'Abd al-Muttalib who is Shabih al-Hamd; and on the side of his mothers' fathers, connected to Mudad ibn 'Amr al-Jurhumi, the grandfather of the males of the children of Ishmael, and through his maternal uncles from al-Khazraj from Salma, the mother of 'Abd al-Muttalib, and from Banu Zuhra through his mother Amina; and he has noble lineages through his mothers' fathers like al-'Awatik, al-Fawatim, and others. Then it is not hidden from scholars of histories and guardians of Arab genealogies and their days, those knowledgeable of their nobles, their generous ones, and their brave ones, that every one whose lineage connects to him was a pillar for his family, a chief of his tribe and group, a master of his clan, distinguished by all virtues, described with praiseworthy qualities and merits. And they were lords of judgment and protection, possessors of watering and guardianship, masters of the assembly hall, and delegates to kings and great ones, honored in their eyes, venerated with them, called among all Arab tribes—Qahtan and 'Adnan, Mudar and Rabi'a, Qays and Khindif—the family of Allah, His neighbors, and inhabitants of His sanctuary. And whoever's lineage is in this state, and his root in honor is this root, his preoccupation with seeking sustenance and fabrication is from the impossible that has no form and the absurd that has no scope in intellects due to its establishment, for that is the action of one who traces back to baseness in origin, lowliness in lineage, meanness in roots, and vileness in morals. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines the Prophet's noble lineage as a proof of his prophethood. It begins by stating that his lineage is a result of Abraham's supplication (Quran 2:129), and explains that the prayer was specifically for a messenger from Ishmael's descendants, which only Muhammad fulfilled. Then it lists the Prophet's ancestors from Ishmael down through specific names, emphasizing their nobility and virtues. It also mentions noble lineages from the maternal side. The passage argues that every ancestor was a leader and possessor of virtues, and that such a lineage makes it impossible that the Prophet would fabricate a message, as that would be characteristic of base lineage. Thus, his noble lineage supports his truthfulness.

Misconception: One might think noble lineage is not necessary for prophethood; Nasafi shows it is a proof of his truthfulness.
Correction: Nasafi argues that the Prophet's lineage is so noble that it would be impossible for him to fabricate a message, as that would be characteristic of base lineages.

The Prophet's lineage, rooted in Ibrahim's prayer and marked by nobility, is a rational proof that he could not have fabricated his message.

?

Are you living in a way that would make your ancestors proud, or are you tarnishing your spiritual lineage?
?
The Prophet's ancestors were described as 'pillars', 'chiefs', and 'masters'—they were people of virtue and leadership. Who is looking up to you as a role model? Are you providing that same pillar of strength and honor to your family, community, and those who follow you?
?

If the Prophet's nobility prevented him from lying, what does your own behavior reveal about your character? Are you living up to the nobility of your faith?

The Prophet's Noble Lineage as Evidence of Truthfulness
The author enumerates the Prophet's noble lineage and argues it precludes falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's noble lineage serves as a circumstantial evidence for his truthfulness in classical Islamic theology.

Core Idea
A noble lineage precludes base acts like false prophecy.

In this passage, the author presents a unique proof of the Prophet's truthfulness: his impeccable ancestry. By examining the noble status of the Prophet's forefathers, the argument shows that someone of such high lineage would never resort to fabricating a divine message for worldly gain. Let us read how the author connects genealogy to moral character.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to understand the overall argument.
2
Identify the lineage details
Note the specific ancestors mentioned: Mudāḍ ibn ʿAmr al-Jurhumī, Salmā, ʿĀmina, and the noble women al-ʿAwātik and al-Fawāṭim.
The author traces the Prophet's lineage through both paternal and maternal lines.
3
Understand the honor of the ancestors
The author describes the ancestors as pillars of their families, chiefs of tribes, and holders of key positions like water-giving, guardianship, and the house of counsel.
These positions were highly respected in pre-Islamic Arab society.
4
Grasp the logical conclusion
The author argues that someone from such a noble lineage would not engage in fabrication or seek sustenance through false prophethood.
This is a form of argument from character (argumentum ad verecundiam reversed).
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this proof fits among other proofs of prophethood (dalā'il al-nubuwwa).
This is one evidence, not the sole proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو شبيه الحمد و من قبل أمهات آبائه متصلاً بمضاض بن عمرو الجرهمي جد ذكورة ولد إسماعيل وبأخواله من الخزرج بسلمى والدة عبد المطلب وبني زهرة بأمه آمنة وله عليه السلام أنساب شريفة من قبل أمهات آبائه كالعواتك والفواطم وغيرهن ثم لا يخفى على العلماء بالتواريخ والحفاظ لأنساب العرب وأيامها العارفين بأشرافهم وأجوادهم وشجعانهم أن كل واحد ممن يتصل نسبه به كان عمادًا لأسرته ورئيسًا لقبيلته وزمرته وسيدًا لعشيرته مخصوصا بجميع الفضائل موصوفًا بالمحامد والمناقب وكانوا أرباب الحكم والرفادة وأصحاب السقاية والسدانة وسادة دار الندوة والوافدين عند الملوك والأجلة المعظمين في أعينهم المتبجلين عندهم المسمين عند جميع قبائل العرب - قحطانها وعدنانها مضرها وربيعها قيسها وخندقها آل الله وجيرانه وسكان حرمه ومن كان حال نسبه هذه الحالة وعرقه في الشرف هذا العرق كان الاشتغال منه بالرزق والافتعال من الممتنع الذي لا تصور له والمحال الذي لا مجال له في العقول لثبوته إذ ذلك فعل من يرجع إلى خساسة في الأصل وضعة في النسب ولؤم في الأعراق ودناءه في الأخلاق وبالله التوفيق.
It is similar to praise, and from the mothers of his fathers connected to Mudāḍ ibn ʿAmr al-Jurhumī, the grandfather of the male descendants of Ismāʿīl, and by his maternal uncles from al-Khazraj, to Salmā, the mother of ʿAbd al-Muṭṭalib, and by Banī Zuhra from his mother Āmina. And he (peace be upon him) has noble lineages from the mothers of his fathers, such as al-ʿAwātik and al-Fawāṭim and others. Then it is not hidden from the scholars of histories and the memorizers of the genealogies of the Arabs and their days, who are knowledgeable of their nobles, their generous ones, and their brave ones, that every one of those whose lineage connects to him was a pillar for his family, a chief of his tribe and his group, a master of his clan, specially endowed with all virtues, described with praiseworthy qualities and noble traits. And they were lords of judgment and provision, possessors of water-giving and guardianship, masters of the house of counsel, and those who present themselves before kings and magnates, revered in their eyes, honored by them, renowned among all the tribes of the Arabs – Qaḥṭān and ʿAdnān, Muḍar and Rabīʿa, Qays and Khindif – as the family of Allah, His neighbors, and the inhabitants of His sanctuary. And whoever has his lineage in this state and his root in honor such as this root, it is impossible that he would occupy himself with seeking sustenance and fabrication, something unimaginable and impossible in the intellects, because that is the act of one who goes back to baseness in origin, lowliness in lineage, vileness in roots, and meanness in character. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an argument from the Prophet's noble lineage. The author begins by detailing the Prophet's ancestry from both paternal and maternal sides, tracing back to Mudāḍ ibn ʿAmr al-Jurhumī, and mentioning noble women like al-ʿAwātik and al-Fawāṭim. He then states that it is well-known to historians and genealogists that every ancestor of the Prophet was a pillar of his family, chief of his tribe, possessed of all virtues. These ancestors held key positions in pre-Islamic Mecca: they were the ones who provided judgment, water, guardianship of the Kaaba, and were the masters of the Dār al-Nadwa (the assembly house). They were highly respected by kings and all Arab tribes. The author then draws the conclusion: since the Prophet comes from such a pure, noble lineage, it is impossible that he would engage in seeking sustenance (i.e., claim prophethood for material gain) or fabricate a message. Such an action would only be expected from someone of base origin and low character. Therefore, the Prophet's impeccable lineage is a strong circumstantial evidence for his truthfulness.

Key Terms
نسب (genealogy)
العواتك (al-ʿAwātik)
الفواطم (al-Fawāṭim)
قبائل العرب (Arab tribes)
دار الندوة (house of counsel)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that noble lineage alone proves prophethood.
Correction: The author uses it as one of several proofs (dalā'il al-nubuwwa), not as a standalone proof.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument in this passage?
A) The Prophet's lineage shows he was from the Quraysh.
B) The Prophet's noble lineage makes it impossible that he would claim prophethood for worldly gain.
C) The Prophet's ancestors were all prophets.
D) The Prophet's lineage is proof that he was a king.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's noble lineage is a strong circumstantial evidence that he could not have fabricated his prophethood for worldly gain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet's noble lineage made it unthinkable for him to lie about prophethood, what does your own 'lineage' of character—your habits, choices, and reputation—say about your truthfulness? Where do you compromise honesty for personal gain, and how can you align your actions with a higher spiritual standard?
?
The passage argues that the Prophet's ancestors were 'pillars for their families' and 'masters of their tribes.' Consider your own role in your family and community: are you a pillar of integrity, generosity, and honor? If not, what concrete step will you take this week to be a source of strength and virtue for those around you?
?
The author says that fabrication is the act of 'one who goes back to baseness in origin and lowliness in lineage.' In what ways might you be tempted to excuse dishonesty in small matters because 'everyone does it' or because you feel your background doesn't matter? How does the Prophet's example demand a higher standard from you, regardless of your family history?

Answered Supplications as Proofs of Prophethood
The author lists several of the Prophet's answered supplications as miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the answered supplications of the Prophet serve as miracles (mu'jizāt) that confirm his prophethood, based on historical examples transmitted by tawātur.

Core Idea
Answered supplications are tangible miracles that prove prophethood.

In this passage, the author presents several instances where the Prophet's supplications were answered in extraordinary ways—drought, political collapse, even a lion attacking an enemy. These are not ordinary coincidences; they are transmitted by numerous chains (tawātur) and provide certain knowledge of his prophethood. Let's examine the examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Notice the list of supplications and their outcomes.
The author begins by stating these are from the category of his du'as.
2
Identify the listed supplications
Count how many examples are given. The author mentions supplications against Muḍar, Kisrā, ʿUtba ibn Abī Lahab, for Ibn ʿAbbās, the cave incident, and the horse's hooves.
Each example is introduced with 'من ذلك' or 'ومنها'.
3
Note the role of tawātur
The author states that the first example (Muḍar) is transmitted by tawātur. This is key: multiple reliable chains confirm these events.
Tawātur guarantees certain knowledge in Islamic epistemology.
4
Reflect on the proof value
Consider why answered supplications are considered miracles. They are beyond normal human capacity and confirm the Prophet's connection to Allah.
These are not ordinary answers to prayer; they involve natural phenomena or historical outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما هو راجع إلى دعواته عليه السلام: فأما ما هو راجع إلى دعواته فمن ذلك دعاؤه على مضر حين آذوه وكذبوه فقال: اللهم أشدد وطأتك على مضر واجعل عليهم سنين كسني يوسف فأمسك عنهم القطر حتى جف النبات والشجر وهلكت المواشي وكان انكشاف الجدب عنهم أيضًا بدعائه فأتاهم الغيث وكثر حتى هدم بيوتهم فكلموه في ذلك فقال: اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا اللهم على الظراب والجبال وبطون الأودية وذلك كله منقول بالتواتر ومن ذلك دعاؤه على كسرى حين مزق كتابه وبعث إليه بتراب فقال: اللهم مزق ملكه كل ممزق وقال لأصحابه: مزق كتابي أما إنه ستمزق أمته وبعث إلي بالتراب أما إنكم ستملكون أرضه فمزق الله ملكه وشتت جمعه وملكهم أرضه ومن ذلك دعاؤه على عتبة بن أبي لهب: اللهم سلط عليه كلبًا من كلابك فافترسه الأسد في بعض أسفاره ومنها دعاؤه لعبد الله بن عباس بالفقه والحكمة رضي الله عنهما فحصل ما دعا ومنها ما أعمى الله تعالى أبصار الظالمين له حين كان في الغار ومنها ما ساخ بقوائم فرس من اتبعه في الأرض بدعائه وفي ذلك كثرة وفي هذا القدر كفاية.
What pertains to his supplications (peace be upon him): As for what pertains to his supplications, among that is his supplication against Muḍar when they harmed him and denied him. He said: 'O Allah, make your punishment severe upon Muḍar, and send upon them years like the years of Joseph.' So He withheld rain from them until plants and trees dried up and livestock perished. The removal of drought from them was also through his supplication, so rain came to them and increased until it destroyed their houses. They spoke to him about that, so he said: 'O Allah, around us and not upon us; O Allah, on the hills, the mountains, and the valleys.' All of that is transmitted by tawātur. Among that also is his supplication against Kisrā when he tore his letter and sent him dirt. He said: 'O Allah, tear his kingdom apart entirely.' And he said to his companions: 'He tore my letter; indeed, his nation will be torn apart. He sent me dirt; indeed, you will conquer his land.' So Allah tore his kingdom, scattered his assembly, and gave them his land. Among that also is his supplication against ʿUtba ibn Abī Lahab: 'O Allah, set upon him a dog from your dogs,' so a lion devoured him on one of his journeys. Among them is his supplication for ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAbbās for understanding and wisdom (may Allah be pleased with him), and what he supplicated for was realized. Among them is that Allah blinded the eyes of the wrongdoers to him when he was in the cave. Among them is that the hooves of a horse of one of his followers sank into the earth through his supplication. There is abundance of that, and in this measure is sufficient.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage lists several answered supplications of the Prophet as miraculous proofs of his prophethood. The author begins by stating that these are from the category of his du'as. He gives five examples: First, the Prophet's supplication against the tribe of Muḍar when they harmed him: he asked for seven years of drought like Prophet Joseph's time, and it happened; then he prayed for its removal, and it was removed, but rain became excessive until they complained, and he prayed for it to be around them, not on them. Second, his supplication against the Persian king Kisrā when he tore his letter: he prayed that God tear apart his kingdom, and it happened, and the Muslims conquered Persia. Third, his supplication against ʿUtba ibn Abī Lahab that a dog would be set upon him, and a lion devoured him. Fourth, his supplication for ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAbbās for knowledge and wisdom, which was granted. Fifth, the incident where Allah blinded the sight of the polytheists when the Prophet was in the cave during the Hijra. Sixth, the miracle of the horse's hooves sinking into the earth. The author concludes that there are many such instances, and these are sufficient as proof.

Key Terms
دعاء (supplication)
تواتر (tawātur: mass transmission)
كسرى (Kisrā: Persian king)
مضر (Muḍar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think these events were ordinary coincidences or natural occurrences.
Correction: The author emphasizes that these are extraordinary events transmitted by tawātur, making them certain proofs of prophethood, not coincidences.

Checkpoint
Which of the following supplications of the Prophet is NOT mentioned in this passage?
A) Against Muḍar for drought.
B) Against the Jews of Khaybar.
C) Against Kisrā for tearing his letter.
D) For ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAbbās for wisdom.

Key Takeaway
The answered supplications of the Prophet, transmitted by tawātur, constitute clear miracles that confirm his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Torah Prophecy of Sinai, Seir, and Paran
Author interprets the Torah verse as referring to the three revelations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Torah verse about Sinai, Seir, and Paran foretells the three major revelations: Torah to Moses, Gospel to Jesus, and Quran to Muhammad.

Core Idea
Three mountains, three revelations, one divine plan.

Scholars of earlier scriptures have compiled many prophecies about the coming of Muhammad. One of the clearest is from the Torah, which speaks of Allah coming from Sinai, shining from Seir, and being revealed from Paran. This passage unpacks the meaning of those locations and shows how they point to Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the Torah verse
Read the Torah verse as quoted by the author: 'Allah came from Sinai, shone from Seir, and was revealed from Paran.' Notice the three locations.
2
Understand the interpretation
The author explains that Sinai corresponds to Moses, Seir to Jesus (from Nazareth), and Paran to Muhammad (Mecca). This is a clear sequence.
This interpretation is supported by the People of the Book.
3
Consider the rhetorical questions
The author asks: what other place named Paran exists besides Mecca? And what prophet came after Jesus other than Muhammad? These questions solidify the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ الكتب السابقة بشرت بنبوته عليه السلام] وأما ما كان راجعًا إلى البشارات الواردة بنبوته فقد أورد العلماء بالكتب المتقدمة أشياء كثيرة، منها ما ذكر في التوراة: "جاء الله تعالى من سيناء، وأشرق من ساعير، واستعلن من جبال فاران (۱) فكان فيه إخبار عن إنزال التوراة على موسى عليه السلام بطور سيناء، وإنزاله الإنجيل على عيسى عليه السلام بساعير فإنه كان يسكن من ساعير بقرية تدعى ناصرة، وباسمها سمى من اتبعه نصاری وإنزاله القرآن على محمد والله بجبال فاران وهي جبال مكة، إذ فاران هي مكة، يقر بذلك أهل الكتاب، فإن فى التوراة أن إبراهيم عليه السلام أسكن هاجر - رضي الله عنها - وإسماعيل عليه السلام فاران ويقال (۱) لهم : ما الموضع الذي استعلن الله منه : فلا ذلك واسمه فاران سوى مكة ؟ ومن النبي الذي أنزل عليه الكتاب بعد عیسی سوی محمد؟ ومنها ما ذكر في التوراة لموسى في السفر الخامس: "إني أقيم لبني إسرائيل نبيًا من إخوتهم مثلك أجعل كلامي على فمه فأخوة بني إسرائيل بنو إسماعيل، كما أن أخوة بكر هم تغلب، وأخوة تغلب، وأخوة عيسى هم ذبيان وأخوة الأوس هم الخزرج، ومثل موسى من الأنبياء ليس إلا نبي الله محمد عليه السلام، لما أنه صاحب شريعة مستأنفة فيها بين مصالح (۳) الدارين، وليس لأحد سواه من الأنبياء بعد موسى يصح صرفهم هذا الكلام إلى بعض أنبياء بني إسرائيل، لما ليس أحد منهم مثل موسى عليه السلام، وكذا هم من أنفسهم لا من إخوتهم ، ألا ترى أن من قال لآخر: ائتني برجل من أخوة بني بكر بن وائل لكان يجب عليه أن يأتيه برجل من بني تغلب لا برجل من بني بكر، ومنها ما ذكر في الزبور "تقلد أيها الجبار السيف فإن ناموسك وشرائعك مقرونة بهيبة يمينك وسهامك (٤) مسنونة والأمم يخرون تحتك" وليس المتقلد للسيف من الأنبياء إلا نبينا محمد عليه السلام، وهو الذي خرت الأمم تحته وقرنت شرائعه بالهيبة ومنها ما قال في الزبور . قال :داود: "اللهم ابعث جاعل السنة حتى يعلم الناس أنه بشر وهذا إخبار عن المسيح وعن محمد عليهما السلام يريد ابعث محمدًا حتى يعلم الناس أن عيسى بشر. فعلم داود أن قوما
[The previous scriptures gave glad tidings of his prophethood] As for what pertains to the glad tidings (bisharat) of his prophethood, the scholars have mentioned many things in the earlier books. Among them is what is mentioned in the Torah: 'Allah came from Sinai, and shone forth from Seir, and was revealed from the mountains of Paran' (1). So in that is information about the revelation of the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, at Mount Sinai; and the revelation of the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, at Seir, for he used to reside in Seir in a village called Nazareth, and by its name those who followed him were called Nazarenes; and the revelation of the Qur'an to Muhammad, peace be upon him, from the mountains of Paran, which are the mountains of Mecca, for Paran is Mecca – the People of the Book acknowledge this, for in the Torah Abraham, peace be upon him, settled Hagar - may Allah be pleased with her - and Ishmael in Paran. And they are asked: 'What place did Allah reveal Himself from other than that? Its name is Paran, other than Mecca? And which prophet was revealed the scripture after Jesus other than Muhammad?' And among them is what is mentioned in the Torah to Moses in the fifth book: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brothers, like you; I will place My words in his mouth' – so the brothers of the Children of Israel are the children of Ishmael, just as the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, and the brothers of Taghlib, and the brothers of 'Isa are Dhubyan, and the brothers of al-Aws are al-Khazraj. And there is no prophet like Moses except the Prophet of Allah, Muhammad, peace be upon him, because he is the possessor of a new law (shari'a) that encompasses the benefits of the two abodes. And there is no one other than him among the prophets after Moses to whom this speech can be applied to some prophet of the Children of Israel, for none of them is like Moses, peace be upon him; also, they are from themselves, not from their brothers. Do you not see that if someone said to another, 'Bring me a man from the brothers of Banu Bakr ibn Wa'il,' he would have to bring him a man from Banu Taghlib, not a man from Banu Bakr? And among them is what is mentioned in the Zabur: 'Gird your sword, O mighty one, for your law and your statutes are accompanied by the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall under you.' And there is no prophet who girded on the sword except our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him; and it is he under whom the nations fell and his laws were accompanied by awe. And among them is what is said in the Zabur. David said: 'O Allah, send the establisher of the sunna until the people know that he is a human' – and this is information about the Messiah and about Muhammad, peace be upon them both. He intended: send Muhammad so that the people know that Jesus is a human. So David knew that a people...
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a collection of prophecies from the Torah and Zabur that foretell the coming of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by stating that scholars have compiled many such prophecies.

The first prophecy is from the Torah (Deuteronomy 33:2): 'Allah came from Sinai, shone forth from Seir, and was revealed from Paran.' The author interprets this as referring to the revelations given to Moses at Sinai, Jesus at Seir (Nazareth), and Muhammad at Paran (Mecca). He argues that Paran is Mecca, citing that Abraham settled Hagar and Ishmael there, which the People of the Book acknowledge. The author presents rhetorical questions: what other place named Paran could it be? And what prophet after Jesus received scripture other than Muhammad?

The second prophecy is from the fifth book of the Torah (Deuteronomy 18:18): 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brothers, like you.' The author explains that 'their brothers' refers to the Ishmaelites, not the Israelites themselves. He draws analogies: just as the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, the brothers of the Israelites are the Ishmaelites. He argues that the only prophet after Moses who was like him (bringing a new law) is Muhammad. No other prophet among the Israelites fits because they are from themselves, not brothers.

The third prophecy is from the Zabur (Psalms 45:3-5): 'Gird your sword, O mighty one...' The author asserts that only Muhammad among the prophets bore a sword and conquered nations, so this applies to him.

The fourth prophecy from the Zabur is a prayer of David: 'O Allah, send the establisher of the sunna until the people know that he is a human.' The author interprets this as a prophecy about Muhammad coming to clarify that Jesus was a human, not divine. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear: David knew that a people would deify Jesus, so he prayed for a prophet to correct that.

Throughout, the author uses linguistic and historical reasoning to prove that these texts can only refer to Muhammad.

Key Terms
توراة
سيناء
ساعير
فاران
بشارات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim Paran refers to a place other than Mecca, or that the verse only refers to the Old Testament.
Correction: The author points out that Paran is identified as Mecca by the People of the Book and that Abraham settled Hagar and Ishmael there, and that the sequence of revelation points to three distinct prophets.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Torah verse about Sinai, Seir, and Paran explicitly predicts the coming of Muhammad as the recipient of the final revelation in Mecca.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Prophecy of a Prophet Like Moses from the Brothers of Israel
Author argues that Deuteronomy 18:18 prophesies Muhammad by identifying 'brothers' as Ishmaelites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Torah's promise of a prophet 'like Moses' from the 'brothers' of Israel uniquely points to Muhammad.

Core Idea
A prophet like Moses must bring a new law — and only Muhammad did.

The Torah contains a well-known prophecy that God would raise up a prophet from among the brothers of Israel, like Moses. The author explains who these 'brothers' are using clear linguistic analogies with Arab tribes, showing that the prophet must come from the Ishmaelites, and the only prophet after Moses who matches the description is Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the Torah quote
Read the quote from Deuteronomy 18:18: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brothers, like you.'
2
Understand the meaning of 'brothers'
The author explains that the 'brothers' of the Israelites are the Ishmaelites, using tribal analogies: just as the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, the brothers of Israel are Ishmael's descendants.
Note the linguistic pattern: 'brothers' refers to a related but distinct tribe.
3
Identify the prophet like Moses
The author argues that only Muhammad is like Moses because he brought a new law (shari'a) covering both this world and the next. No other post-Mosaic prophet fits.
4
Apply the tribal analogy
The author gives a concrete example: if someone asks for a man from the brothers of Banu Bakr, you bring a man from Taghlib, not from Bakr. Similarly, the prophet from the brothers of Israel must come from the Ishmaelites, not the Israelites.

Throughout, the author uses linguistic and historical reasoning to prove that these texts can only refer to Muhammad.

The Zabur Prophecies: The Sword-Bearing Prophet and David's Prayer
Author cites two Zabur prophecies pointing to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Psalms of David foretell Muhammad as the sword-bearing prophet and the one who clarifies Jesus's humanity.

Core Idea
The Psalms describe a warrior prophet and a prayer for truth about Jesus — both point to Muhammad.

The Zabur (Psalms) also contains prophecies about the coming of Muhammad. One psalm speaks of a mighty one girding his sword, with nations falling under him. Another records David's prayer for the establisher of the sunna so that people know Jesus is human. The author argues these uniquely apply to Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the first Zabur quote
Read the quote: 'Gird your sword, O mighty one, for your law and your statutes are accompanied by the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall under you.'
2
Identify the sword-bearing prophet
The author notes that among the prophets, only Muhammad bore a sword in conquest. This fits the description of a warrior prophet.
3
Read the second Zabur quote
Read David's prayer: 'O Allah, send the establisher of the sunna until the people know that he is a human.'
4
Understand the purpose of this prayer
The author interprets this as a prophecy about Muhammad coming to clarify that Jesus is human, countering the deification that would occur.
David foresaw that some would deify Jesus, so he prayed for a prophet to correct this.

[The previous scriptures gave glad tidings of his prophethood] As for what pertains to the glad tidings (bisharat) of his prophethood, the scholars have mentioned many things in the earlier books. Among them is what is mentioned in the Torah: 'Allah came from Sinai, and shone forth from Seir, and was revealed from the mountains of Paran' (1). So in that is information about the revelation of the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, at Mount Sinai; and the revelation of the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, at Seir, for he used to reside in Seir in a village called Nazareth, and by its name those who followed him were called Nazarenes; and the revelation of the Qur'an to Muhammad, peace be upon him, from the mountains of Paran, which are the mountains of Mecca, for Paran is Mecca – the People of the Book acknowledge this, for in the Torah Abraham, peace be upon him, settled Hagar - may Allah be pleased with her - and Ishmael in Paran. And they are asked: 'What place did Allah reveal Himself from other than that? Its name is Paran, other than Mecca? And which prophet was revealed the scripture after Jesus other than Muhammad?' And among them is what is mentioned in the Torah to Moses in the fifth book: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brothers, like you; I will place My words in his mouth' – so the brothers of the Children of Israel are the children of Ishmael, just as the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, and the brothers of Taghlib, and the brothers of 'Isa are Dhubyan, and the brothers of al-Aws are al-Khazraj. And there is no prophet like Moses except the Prophet of Allah, Muhammad, peace be upon him, because he is the possessor of a new law (shari'a) that encompasses the benefits of the two abodes. And there is no one other than him among the prophets after Moses to whom this speech can be applied to some prophet of the Children of Israel, for none of them is like Moses, peace be upon him; also, they are from themselves, not from their brothers. Do you not see that if someone said to another, 'Bring me a man from the brothers of Banu Bakr ibn Wa'il,' he would have to bring him a man from Banu Taghlib, not a man from Banu Bakr? And among them is what is mentioned in the Zabur: 'Gird your sword, O mighty one, for your law and your statutes are accompanied by the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall under you.' And there is no prophet who girded on the sword except our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him; and it is he under whom the nations fell and his laws were accompanied by awe. And among them is what is said in the Zabur. David said: 'O Allah, send the establisher of the sunna until the people know that he is a human' – and this is information about the Messiah and about Muhammad, peace be upon them both. He intended: send Muhammad so that the people know that Jesus is a human. So David knew that a people...
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a collection of prophecies from the Torah and Zabur that foretell the coming of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by stating that scholars have compiled many such prophecies.

The first prophecy is from the Torah (Deuteronomy 33:2): 'Allah came from Sinai, shone forth from Seir, and was revealed from Paran.' The author interprets this as referring to the revelations given to Moses at Sinai, Jesus at Seir (Nazareth), and Muhammad at Paran (Mecca). He argues that Paran is Mecca, citing that Abraham settled Hagar and Ishmael there, which the People of the Book acknowledge. The author presents rhetorical questions: what other place named Paran could it be? And what prophet after Jesus received scripture other than Muhammad?

The second prophecy is from the fifth book of the Torah (Deuteronomy 18:18): 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brothers, like you.' The author explains that 'their brothers' refers to the Ishmaelites, not the Israelites themselves. He draws analogies: just as the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, the brothers of the Israelites are the Ishmaelites. He argues that the only prophet after Moses who was like him (bringing a new law) is Muhammad. No other prophet among the Israelites fits because they are from themselves, not brothers.

The third prophecy is from the Zabur (Psalms 45:3-5): 'Gird your sword, O mighty one...' The author asserts that only Muhammad among the prophets bore a sword and conquered nations, so this applies to him.

The fourth prophecy from the Zabur is a prayer of David: 'O Allah, send the establisher of the sunna until the people know that he is a human.' The author interprets this as a prophecy about Muhammad coming to clarify that Jesus was a human, not divine. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear: David knew that a people would deify Jesus, so he prayed for a prophet to correct that.

Throughout, the author uses linguistic and historical reasoning to prove that these texts can only refer to Muhammad.

زبور
تقلد السيف
جاعل السنة
بشر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the sword prophecy refers to David or Jesus, or that David's prayer is about a general reformer.
Correction: The author argues that only Muhammad girded the sword and conquered nations, and David's specific prayer was for the one who would clarify that Jesus is human.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Psalms predict Muhammad as a sword-bearing conqueror and as the one who will correct the exaggeration about Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Prophecy from Seir and Paran
Interpreting a biblical theophany as prophecy of the three revelations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a biblical verse about God appearing from Seir and Paran is interpreted as prophesying the revelations to Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
The mountains of Paran point to Mecca and the Qur'anic revelation.

The author begins by citing a well-known biblical passage about God's appearance from Sinai, Seir, and Paran. He interprets each location as a signpost for the major revelations: the Torah given to Moses at Sinai, the Gospel to Jesus in Seir (Nazareth), and the Qur'an to Muhammad at Paran (Mecca). This sets the stage for the other prophecies that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the three locations
Read the passage carefully and identify the three locations mentioned: Sinai, Seir, and Paran. Notice how the author connects each to a prophet and scripture.
2
Understand the connection to each prophet
The author argues that Sinai refers to Moses and the Torah, Seir to Jesus and the Gospel, and Paran to Muhammad and the Qur'an. Reflect on why he makes these specific associations.
3
Reflect on the significance of Paran as Mecca
The author asserts that Paran is Mecca, citing the settlement of Hagar and Ishmael. Consider how this supports the prophecy of the Qur'an's revelation in Mecca.

From Seir, and He shone forth from Mount Paran, and in it there is news of the sending down of the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, at Mount Sinai, and the sending down of the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, at Seir, for he used to live in Seir in a village called Nazareth, and by its name those who followed him were called Christians, and the sending down of the Qur'an to Muhammad, peace be upon him, at the mountains of Paran, which are the mountains of Mecca, for Paran is Mecca, the People of the Book affirm this. And among them are many expressions in the Gospel by the name 'Faraqlit' (Paraclete), such as that the Paraclete is the Spirit of Truth whom He sends in my name, He will teach you everything. The scholars have mentioned in their books these expressions and many things from the books of the earlier prophets, peace be upon them, containing mention of him, and mention of his companions, and mention of Mecca, the Kaaba, the sanctuary, the stone, and other things. The people of the two Books do not deny the establishment of that, but they distort words from their places and interpret all of that with unnatural, corrupt interpretations to other than what is intended.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage collects scriptural prophecies from the Torah, Psalms, and Gospel that foretell the coming of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins with a verse from the Torah describing God's appearance at Sinai, Seir, and Paran, interpreting Paran as Mecca and thus indicating the revelation of the Qur'an in Mecca. He then cites the prophecy in Deuteronomy of a prophet from the brothers of Israel, arguing that 'brothers' means the Ishmaelites, not Israelites, and that only Muhammad fits the description of a law-giving prophet like Moses. Logical analogies are given to support this interpretation. Next, he quotes Psalm verses about girding a sword and peoples falling under him, applied to Muhammad as the warrior prophet. Another Psalm verse about 'the establisher of the Sunnah' is interpreted to mean that people will learn from Muhammad that Jesus was human, countering later Christian claims of divinity. Finally, he references Gospel mentions of the Paraclete, identified as Muhammad. The passage concludes by noting that Jews and Christians do not deny these texts but distort their meanings.

Exegesis of the Deuteronomy prophecy of a prophet like Moses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophecy in Deuteronomy about a prophet from the brothers of Israel and why it is fulfilled by Muhammad.

Core Idea
'Brothers of Israel' means the Ishmaelites, not the Israelites.

The author now turns to a famous prophecy in Deuteronomy where God promises to raise up a prophet like Moses from among the brothers of the Children of Israel. Through linguistic and historical analysis, he demonstrates that 'brothers' refers to the Ishmaelites, the descendants of Ishmael, and that only Muhammad matches the description of a law-giving prophet like Moses.

Guided Path
1
Read the prophecy and the author's interpretation
Read the Deuteronomy quote and notice how the author interprets 'brothers of Israel' as the Ishmaelites, using tribal analogies.
2
Understand the linguistic argument about 'brothers'
The author gives examples from Arab tribes: the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, not Bakr themselves. Similarly, the brothers of Israel are the Ishmaelites.
3
See why only Muhammad fits the description
The author argues that only Muhammad came with a new law like Moses, and no Israelite prophet after Moses was like him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من ساعير، واستعلن من جبال فاران فكان فيه إخبار عن إنزال التوراة على موسى عليه السلام بطور سيناء، وإنزاله الإنجيل على عيسى عليه السلام بساعير فإنه كان يسكن من ساعير بقرية تدعى ناصرة، وباسمها سمى من اتبعه نصاری وإنزاله القرآن على محمد عليه السلام بجبال فاران وهي جبال مكة، إذ فاران هي مكة، يقر بذلك أهل الكتاب، فإن فى التوراة أن إبراهيم عليه السلام أسكن هاجر - رضي الله عنها - وإسماعيل عليه السلام فاران ويقال لهم : ما الموضع الذي استعلن الله منه : فلا ذلك واسمه فاران سوى مكة ؟ ومن النبي الذي أنزل عليه الكتاب بعد عیسی سوی محمد؟ ومنها ما ذكر في التوراة لموسى في السفر الخامس: "إني أقيم لبني إسرائيل نبيًا من إخوتهم مثلك أجعل كلامي على فمه فأخوة بني إسرائيل بنو إسماعيل، كما أن أخوة بكر هم تغلب، وأخوة تغلب، وأخوة عيسى هم ذبيان وأخوة الأوس هم الخزرج، ومثل موسى من الأنبياء ليس إلا نبي الله محمد عليه السلام، لما أنه صاحب شريعة مستأنفة فيها بين مصالح الدارين، وليس لأحد سواه من الأنبياء بعد موسى يصح صرفهم هذا الكلام إلى بعض أنبياء بني إسرائيل، لما ليس أحد منهم مثل موسى عليه السلام، وكذا هم من أنفسهم لا من إخوتهم ، ألا ترى أن من قال لآخر: ائتني برجل من أخوة بني بكر بن وائل لكان يجب عليه أن يأتيه برجل من بني تغلب لا برجل من بني بكر، ومنها ما ذكر في الزبور "تقلد أيها الجبار السيف فإن ناموسك وشرائعك مقرونة بهيبة يمينك وسهامك مسنونة والأمم يخرون تحتك" وليس المتقلد للسيف من الأنبياء إلا نبينا محمد عليه السلام، وهو الذي خرت الأمم تحته وقرنت شرائعه بالهيبة ومنها ما قال في الزبور . قال داود: "اللهم ابعث جاعل السنة حتى يعلم الناس أنه بشر وهذا إخبار عن المسيح وعن محمد عليهما السلام يريد ابعث محمدًا حتى يعلم الناس أن عيسى بشر. فعلم داود أن قوما سيدعون للمسيح ما ادعوا . ومنها ألفاظ كثيرة في الإنجيل باسم فارقليط من ذلك أن الفارقليط روح الحق الذي يرسله أي باسمي هو يعلمك كل شيء. ذكر العلماء بكتبهم هذه الألفاظ وأشياء كثيرة من كتب الأنبياء المتقدمين عليهم السلام فيها ذكره وذكر أصحابه وذكر مكة والكعبة والحرم والحجر وغير ذلك لا ينكر أهل الكتابين ثبوت ذلك غير أنهم يحرفون الكلم من مواضعه ويصرفون ذلك كله بتأويلات مستكرهة فاسدة إلى غير ما هو المراد.
From Seir, and He shone forth from Mount Paran, and in it there is news of the sending down of the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, at Mount Sinai, and the sending down of the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, at Seir, for he used to live in Seir in a village called Nazareth, and by its name those who followed him were called Christians, and the sending down of the Qur'an to Muhammad, peace be upon him, at the mountains of Paran, which are the mountains of Mecca, for Paran is Mecca, the People of the Book affirm this. For in the Torah, Abraham, peace be upon him, settled Hagar - may God be pleased with her - and Ishmael, peace be upon him, in Paran, and it is said to them: What is the place from which God shone forth? Then that, its name is Paran, other than Mecca? And which prophet received the Scripture after Jesus other than Muhammad? And among them is what is mentioned in the Torah to Moses in the fifth book: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brothers like you, and I will put my words in his mouth'; so the brothers of the Children of Israel are the children of Ishmael, just as the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, and the brothers of Taghlib, and the brothers of Jesus are Dhubyan, and the brothers of Aws are Khazraj. And a prophet like Moses among the prophets is only the Prophet of God Muhammad, peace be upon him, because he is the possessor of a new law containing the interests of the two abodes, and there is none other than him among the prophets after Moses to whom this statement can be properly applied to some prophets of the Children of Israel, because none of them is like Moses, peace be upon him, and also they are from themselves, not from their brothers. Do you not see that if someone says to another: Bring me a man from the brothers of Banu Bakr bin Wa'il, he would have to bring him a man from Banu Taghlib, not a man from Banu Bakr. And among them is what is mentioned in the Psalms: 'Gird your sword, O mighty one, for your law and your statutes are accompanied by the majesty of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and nations fall under you.' And the one who girded the sword among the prophets is only our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, and he is the one under whom nations fell, and his laws were accompanied by majesty. And among them is what David said in the Psalms: 'O God, send the establisher of the Sunnah so that people may know that he is human,' and this is news about the Messiah and about Muhammad, peace be upon them both; he intended: send Muhammad so that people may know that Jesus is human. Thus David knew that a people would claim for the Messiah what they claimed. And among them are many expressions in the Gospel by the name 'Faraqlit' (Paraclete), such as that the Paraclete is the Spirit of Truth whom He sends in my name, He will teach you everything. The scholars have mentioned in their books these expressions and many things from the books of the earlier prophets, peace be upon them, containing mention of him, and mention of his companions, and mention of Mecca, the Kaaba, the sanctuary, the stone, and other things. The people of the two Books do not deny the establishment of that, but they distort words from their places and interpret all of that with unnatural, corrupt interpretations to other than what is intended.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage collects scriptural prophecies from the Torah, Psalms, and Gospel that foretell the coming of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins with a verse from the Torah describing God's appearance at Sinai, Seir, and Paran, interpreting Paran as Mecca and thus indicating the revelation of the Qur'an in Mecca. He then cites the prophecy in Deuteronomy of a prophet from the brothers of Israel, arguing that 'brothers' means the Ishmaelites, not Israelites, and that only Muhammad fits the description of a law-giving prophet like Moses. Logical analogies are given to support this interpretation. Next, he quotes Psalm verses about girding a sword and peoples falling under him, applied to Muhammad as the warrior prophet. Another Psalm verse about 'the establisher of the Sunnah' is interpreted to mean that people will learn from Muhammad that Jesus was human, countering later Christian claims of divinity. Finally, he references Gospel mentions of the Paraclete, identified as Muhammad. The passage concludes by noting that Jews and Christians do not deny these texts but distort their meanings.

Key Terms
إخوة
بني إسرائيل
مثل موسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the prophecy refers to a prophet from among the Israelites themselves.
Correction: The author shows that 'brothers' means a different lineage, i.e., the Ishmaelites, and no Israelite prophet after Moses was like him.

Checkpoint
According to the author, who are the 'brothers' of the Children of Israel?
A) The Israelites themselves
B) The Ishmaelites
C) The Edomites
D) The Moabites

Key Takeaway
The prophecy of a prophet like Moses from the brothers of Israel is fulfilled by Muhammad, who brought a new divine law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were challenged today by someone who says the prophecy of a prophet like Moses refers to Joshua, could you clearly explain the 'brothers of Israel' argument? What steps will you take to memorize this reasoning so you can defend the truth confidently?
?
Do you truly believe that Muhammad (peace be upon him) is the prophet like Moses, bringing a complete law? If this belief is solid, how does it affect your obedience to that law in areas where you struggle? If it is not solid, what is holding you back from full conviction?
?
The author uses everyday tribal analogies to make a profound point. Are you willing to use similar clear, logical arguments when speaking about Islam to others, or do you rely on vague impressions? Commit today to learn one logical proof from this lesson and share it with someone this week.

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
The Warrior Prophet in the Psalms
Interpretation of a Psalm verse as prophecy of Muhammad's military success.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a Psalm verse about girding a sword and nations falling under him is applied to Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Psalm's sword-wielding conqueror is Muhammad, who subdued nations.

The author moves to a Psalm verse that describes a mighty warrior girding a sword, with nations falling under him. He argues that among the prophets, only Muhammad was a warrior who fought and conquered, and his laws were established with majesty and awe.

Guided Path
1
Read the Psalm quote
Read the Psalm verse and note its imagery: a sword, majesty, arrows, and falling nations.
2
Understand why the author applies it to Muhammad
The author states that only Muhammad girded the sword among the prophets, implying military conquest.
3
Note the significance of the sword imagery
This prophecy highlights Muhammad's role as a leader who established his religion through both spiritual and temporal power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Psalm describes a prophet whose law is accompanied by majesty and might. How does your own commitment to the shari'ah reflect that same sense of honor and strength, or have you reduced it to mere rituals and rules? What step will you take today to live the shari'ah with dignity and power?
?
Muhammad girded a real sword and subdued nations for the truth. In what area of your life are you still unwilling to 'gird your sword'—to take decisive action for Allah? What fear or comfort holds you back, and when will you move?
?
The verse says nations fall under him. Are you actively contributing to the spread of Islam in your community, or are you content to let others lead while you remain passive? What one concrete action will you take this week to subdue the nations around you, starting with your own household?
